\item \emph{CpuDuration} MUST be present and MUST contain a time duration as defined in ISO 8601:2004\cite{wolf1998date}.
18 18 
\end{itemize}

\subsection{WallDuration}


  		





  21
  25
  
    

  		





  22
  26
  
    
WallClock time elapsed during the job execution. In the case of MPI \emph{WallDuration} might be lower than \emph{CpuDuration}.


  		





  ......




  24
  28

  29
  
    
\end{itemize}

\subsection{StartTime}


  		





  28
  36
  
    

  		





  29
  37
  
    
This property describes a timestamp indicating the time at which the measured resource consumption started. Together with \emph{EndTime} this defines a period over which the resource has been consumed.


  		





  ......




  33
  41
  
    
\item The time zone may be specified as Z (UTC) or (+|-)hh:mm. Time zones that are not specified are considered undetermined.


  		





  34
  42
  
    
\end{itemize}


  		





  35
  43
  
    

  		





  
  44
  
    
\begin{XMLexample}


  		





  
  45
  
    
<ur:StartTime>2013-05-31T11:00:00</ur:StartTime>


  		





  
  46
  
    
\end{XMLexample}


  		





  
  47

  48
  
    
\subsection{EndTime}


  		





  37
  49
  
    

  		





  38
  50
  
    
This property describes a timestamp indicating the time at which the measured resource consumption ended. Together with \emph{StartTime} this defines a period over which the resource has been consumed.


  		





  ......




  42
  54
  
    
\item The time zone may be specified as Z (UTC) or (+|-)hh:mm. Time zones that are not specified are considered undetermined.


  		





  43
  55
  
    
\end{itemize}

  61
  
    
\subsection{Host}


  		





  46
  62
  
    

  		





  47
  63
  
    
This is used to identify the host where the user consumed the resource. As an example, in case of MPI jobs more than one Host parameter can be specified. If a master node for the computation can be identified, it can be flagged as ``primary'' with a dedicated attribute. The \emph{processId} attribute SHOULD be used to identify the process ID of the process running at the host. For example this is required in case of MPI jobs that use multiple hosts.


  		





  ......




  63
  79
  
    
\item The \emph{HostType} field type MUST be a string.


  		





  64
  80
  
    
\end{itemize}


  		





  65
  81

  84
  
    
\end{XMLexample}

\subsection{NodeCount}


  		





  77
  101
  
    

  		





  78
  102
  
    
Number of nodes used. A node definition may be dependent on the architecture, but typically a node is a physical machine. For example a cluster of 16 physical machines with each machine having one processor each is a 16 ``node'' machine, each with one ``processor''. A 16 processor SMP machine however, is 1 physical node (machine) with 16 processors.


  		





  79
  103
  
    
\begin{itemize}


  		





  80
  104
  
    
\item The \emph{NodeCount} value MUST be of type Non-zero Integer


  		





  81
  105
  
    
\end{itemize}

\subsection{JobName}


  		





  29

  30

This attribute may contain a descriptive of the job. It has to be stressed that user defined job names are often difficult to retrieve from an accounting perspective and are not suitable for reliable accounting purposes.

\subsection{Middleware}


  		





  68
  94
  
    

  		





  69
  95
  
    
The purpose of this element is to mark whether the job was submitted locally or through a grid middleware. At least the values ``local'' and ``grid'' MUST be supported. The description attribute SHOULD be used to give additional information on the used middleware.


  		





  ......




  75
  101

  76
  102
  
    
\end{itemize}

  106
  
    
\end{XMLexample}

This element may be used to insert in the records any time instant related to the user payload. Three optional values for the type attribute are defined as they are of common usage by batch systems. The semantic is derived from Torque.

\subsection{Site}


  		





  30

  39
  
    
This property describes the site at which the resource is located. This property should contain a descriptive name of the group of resources which are accounted for in the record. The \emph{Site} value should be constructed in such a way that it is unique within the context where it is used.


  		





  ......




  34
  42

\subsection{GlobalGroupId}


  		





  43
  47
  
    

  		





  44
  48
  
    
This property describes the global group accountable for the resource consumption. The property should identify the group globally, such that clashes do not happen accidentally, e.g. using a FQDN to construct it. In Grid terms, this would typically be the VO name.


  		





  ......




  46
  50
  
    
\item The \emph{GlobalGroupId} field type MUST be a string.


  		





  47
  51
  
    
\end{itemize}


  		





  48
  52
  
    

  		





  
  53
  
    
\begin{XMLexample}


  		





  
  54
  
    
<ur:GlobalGroupId>"binarydataproject.example.org"</ur:GlobalGroupId>


  		





  
  55
  
    
\end{XMLexample}

  49
  57
  
    
\subsection{GlobalGroupAttribute}


  		





  50
  58
  
    

  		





  51
  59
  
    
This property describes supplemental traits of the group property, e.g., sub-groups, role or authority. This makes it possible to account for segments of a group, while still being able to account for the group as a whole. The property consists of a type which denotes the type of attribute and an actual value for the attribute.


  		





  ......




  56
  64
  
    
\item The \emph{GlobalGroupAttribute} type MUST have the type string.


  		





  57
  65
  
    
\item The \emph{GlobalGroupAttribute} field type MUST be a string.


  		





  58
  66
  
    
\end{itemize}


  		





  
  67
  
    

  		





  
  68
  
    
\begin{XMLexample}


  		





  
  69
  
    
<ur:GlobalGroupAttribute ur:type="subgroup">ukusers</ur:GlobalGroupAttribute>


  		





  
  70
  
    
\end{XMLexample}
